Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes, and it is wrapped and gives putrid and corrupt matter, so you must prove all the subtlety of the tent, and take care to know how deep it has gone. Then heat the cauterization that seems appropriate, and apply it to the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and continue the cauterization until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned away, once, twice, or three times, according to the need of the body; and be careful not to harm the nearby nerves and large veins. If the fistula goes to the bladder and intestines, beware of these places, and do not make false passages in the flesh, and think that it is not a permanent injury; after curing the flesh so it is healthy, and if the wounds are well-scraped, and the matters are removed at length, then know that the flesh is entirely healthy; and if the matters are not removed, know that the flesh is troubled, and corrupts the bone in its foundation; and thus one of these things we will discuss in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of the loin comes from cold and great windiness, and does not take heed of a woman, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization to the loins on one side and the other to the clavicle, as we have previously mentioned; and if we make a thousand cauterizations in a row, they will be more effective.
de la vessie	of the vessel
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the vessel is tender and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you make a fire cautery on the affected part above the vessel, where the hairs of the finger begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cautery as long as our thumb; and you make a cautery above the back, or two if you need them; and let the cauteries be made according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow it to conceive, and the flowers are corrupted and their terminations delayed; and when they come, then you feel great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the belly, as we have said or like a cautery of the vessel, and two cauteries above the back; and let the cauteries be made according to the form mentioned before.
de la hainche	of the handle
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the handle of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the places of departure are twisted, so you must cautery the patient on the handle of the hip at the circle, and mark before the joint surrounding the handle as it turns, so that the handle is within the circle; and if the cauteries are such as those with which one has cautered the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present for you, make three cauteries of the large olives, and let the cauteries be as deeply set as all the veins; and treat until it is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hollow of the thigh, and it's from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we said in the division and the cure is worthless, and the disease is ancient: then it's necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills, or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery; and the method of fire cautery is according to eleven methods: it's to know that it assembles burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is according to many methods, one of which is such: that you apply cautery on the hollow of the thigh in three triangular shapes, and make a good profundity and greatness, and leave between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; no one makes cautery in the middle on the top of the thigh, because there is eleven according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if you apply cautery to the cautery of the circle that we mentioned before in the dislocation of the thigh; but do it in such a way that the circles encompass the entire thigh, and all the spaces of the skin are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method that one uses in sciatica, when pain holds in the thigh, and does not reach just to the knee nor just to the leg. And if it reaches the knee and the leg, make three cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds, and one cautery above the ankle two fingers, a little to the left side; and let the cauteries be cutellaire, and let the skin be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends just to two toes or near the ankle, make three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the mastery is, do it more; and if you know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, do fire cautery on the cuticular or circular cautery, and take good care in all your cauteries that you do not leave a single one so much that you burn the nerves and great arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great annoyance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who have performed cautery on the hollow of the foot, and they left it so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the feet also, and were pierced and corrupted to the point that the feet were. After a burst of belly which he got death.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parties together, do cautery on one and on the other, in this manner. // And the wise men said in the cautery of the thigh, that it is in this way, make a fire so sharp and so thick as a navillon of a date, or a little less, and be between the interstices and be from one interstice to another spacing the quantity of a thumb's breadth; and let the interstices be above two parts, and let them also be like nails, and have a well-made iron handle; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated so that it becomes completely red and gives off a sweet smell, and then place it on the box of the thigh of the patient, and turn it around the healthy side; and cautery once with a round cautery rod and leave it for three days; and then make an emplaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until he is healthy.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Here is the translation:
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from a fall or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar matters of cold expanded material, none of these similarities is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after that the patient is void of foul pills or other similar things, that one makes on their back, there where the pain holds, three lines marked with an inch, and in each line 5 cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can suffer; and let the cauterization be made according to the cauterizer called "poins"; and if you see, make 3 cauterizations or 4 at the cauterizing claw in the middle, according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a withered arm when they lift it, and fear; and you find in the upper spine of the back and in our appearance which comes onto the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, then cauterize with a cautery of that kind according to this method.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	If the cautery should burn each part of the spine equally. And if you want to cauterize around the spine with a poignant cautery, draw .ij. lines, and let the points be near one another. After curing the limb so that it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not misapply the cautery in weakness which is in the region of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	from the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints is from moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the foot, which the doctor properly calls "podagra", and when it is caused by cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make a mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need to prick on the face of the foot, then have a complete cautery made at each point that is claimed. And if the pains come right up to the knees and other joints, and this happens often, then have a cautery made on each knee, two or three cauteries for each part, with all the complete cautery olive; and if you have mastery of more, then do more, but do not hold your hand firmer than necessary, as long as the espé of the heart is at rest.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend right up to the knees and back, then administer the cautery that we have spoken of in this chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the finger .ij. lines; and if there remains some pain in the fingers, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come right up to the sides or right up to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and make good government for the patient and prepare medicines. For if you make good government and you purge fleum, then he will be healthy with the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the spleen
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in anger, and the swelling falls to the hips and it's new, if it happens that when you want to cure, he does not eat during the day; and he uses things that ease the stomach, so the farts come out of his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his arm as long as the swelling is repaired, and you massage with your fingers, and anoint beneath the rupture on the bone of the thumb, and all signs are similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	as long as it is white and he casts out sensations. Then massage the swellings to their place; and the ministers hold his hand so they do not turn back; and work well on the hips of the patient, and put beneath him a cushion and a sheet on the hips, and another on the pis who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, so recommence yet another until you come just to the bone; and beware subtly that the swelling does not burst when you do the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that by this the patient may not die, or other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your operations are worth nothing. And it happens that the cauteries of children should be subtle according to the measure of their age, and of great people also according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery of butter so that the inflammation is lifted; after cure other ointments so that he is healthy, and cast the patient twenty days on his back so that the wound is well sucked; and it happens that his nourishments should be relaxed for a long time, so that the swelling does not burst when he prepares to go into chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, instruct him to make a well-made splint, and for forty other days; and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against too great repletion of drinking and eating, and too high pride; and when he does this instruction, he will be entirely healthy. And I will describe the treatment of surgery in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are conjoined, and you see that they do not grow anymore, make them a .j. cautery of the cautery wound according to its quantity, and let it be burned by the third of the heart; after the treatment according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one should cauterize at the cautery at .iij. angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But first sign the place of the incision and make a line for the width above the rupture, and another below, and hold your hand in all the cauterized area with a gentle touch. But the first cauterizations are lighter and more moderate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from chronic pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in no member, either from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no value, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length and smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and of its pain. If it is healthy from the first cautery, that's good; if not, recommence another cautery on top of that one, for such is the custom that it should be moved to the member that is next to it, because it must be that you do the cauteries until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	of messiness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The messes are often helped by cautery with great aid, and especially the illness that comes from the putrefaction of blood and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take care that the illness is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the entire patient, then you do five cauteries on the chief: one in the middle of the head, and another towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and leave it so long as the cauteries come just to the bone, and so that the scabs issue forth if the vapors of the gross humors can issue forth; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the sickness is scattered throughout; it pertains manifestly, so it is necessary that you apply cauterization to these cauterizations that we have mentioned above, and one cautery on each nipple, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and three cauteries on the spine of the back, and one great one on the chest and another delicate one, and two on the shoulders, and two on the hips, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the rear calcifying, so you do not burn them; and never make a cautery on the bone of the finger, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more you do cauterization, the more it helps and is profitable; and know that the patients do not feel any pain from cauterization as the healthy ones feel it, because the body is already almost corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the iron tools. After curing with flour poultice mixed with honey and other treatments until they are healthy.
de enfleure	of inflammation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors. de albaras	of the cauteries
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is enveloped, and the engines of medicine are worthless, then cauterize with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color is changed; then treat with flour of veal and lentils with oil of roses and leaves of plantain, and blood of colon and blood of almonds, each a part; and mix all together, and tie with a bandage, and apply to the skin until it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer begins to develop, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with a cautery that seems like a circle around the tumor. And some wise men say that one should make a cautery at the middle of the cancer; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never wanted it to happen; and the more correct thing is that it be cauterized around, with a cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When some people have a disease called "adubelati", and it delays healing or because of the excessive flow it makes or because of the old age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too weak) and he has little blood, or because of the tension; and you see hasten to heal: then cauterize extensively with many small cauteries pricking; afterwards let it be so. For it will hasten healing.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that the cautery is penetrating everywhere, heat the cautery to the point where its form is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" so that the cauteries penetrate the heart, and let them be such that the patient feels relief in some manner that the course of the disease is alleviated. Afterwards, cure until it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease which is called "corrodens" and it's nothing other than a gangrene of a limb, because it eats away the members like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this disease in someone who can suffer cautery along with fire, then heat the small and large cauteries according to what is needed for the person or the disease; after cauterizing all parts until you burn out all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it two days, and apply cauteries suffering burning with oil until the burns from fire are removed, and all the corruption. After the treatment of wounds producing flesh.  And if you see after two days that healthy flesh does not grow, it's good; and if not, then restart the cautery on what remains of the corrupted limbs. And this gangrene has often been cured by medicine along with fire cautery in place of fire cautery; but always fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of medicine in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of ulcers that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that the feet are affected by a disease which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it's a large swollen thing that ulcerates the foot. And the cauteries of this disease are in two ways. It's known as fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is when you heat one cautery like a pen of velvet, and make it from good iron to the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and that it has subtle margins; after putting everything hot on the ulcer, and turning your hand entirely around the ulcer as much as it comes to the font of the ulcer; and leave it thus for two days until it begins to putrefy; then make a plaster of mild sage boiled with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the ulcers will be cleared and separated from their roots. Then treat the wound with ointment, making it healthy flesh.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by deficient humors of the body, and often occur in many places and on the feet, it is necessary that you apply warm water cautery; and this is how: take a cane of iron or a pointed awl, or a knife of boxwood, and place it on the nail and the joint, which is to say piercing the veins; and place the cane so that it surrounds everything entirely, then put a little warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and then find the warm water pathway deep into the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the warm water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will uproot everything to its roots. Thus do one after another until you have pulled out all those that are in the body, then cure the ulcers that cause heat.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from cold or nerves, or from quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you do four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one cautery or foot, and one on the stomach for an olivaire cautery; if you leave the trembling, and hasten the health of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of small boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	At no time appear by default the corrupt bodies, or small boils, that come from gross corrupted matters. if it is necessary at first when they appear that one do cautery on each head of the boil: a subtle cautery of wood of myrtle, of which the point is taken in fire, or of root of aristologe long, or of lenticular cautery. And at no time are they cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot increase in advance, but are disencumbered of the superfluities from which they come, and are healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great removals of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from corrupt bodies, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever it happens to nobody, if you hasten to put your finger index on the wound of the vein, and hold strongly as long as the blood is appeased beneath your finger, and does not issue more; then put fire cautery, olive oil or more small and large as they are all red; then take .i., big or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is routed, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery strongly until the blood is restored.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it happens to flee when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this one after the other until the blood is stopped; and beware that you do not hurt the nerve that is nearby, and that another evil does not come upon the patient; and know that when the blood flows out of the artery, it cannot be well restored unless it is by one of the three ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied which have power to restore blood; and so it is tied and held in place immediately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers restoration of the constricted blood by applying tight bandages or putting things in, or similar things, does not profit from it at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to none and he does not have better medicine present, then he must put his finger index on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch well so that it is restored above the wound and above the vein; and do not move the finger, but let the frost of cold water often be very cold so that the blood is congealed and thickened and restored; and make an inquiry beforehand about what he needs of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have said in the first chapter all about the disease where it is necessary to use fire cautery, or medicine burning, and the instruments and causes and materials and forms of cauteries; and I put that chapter among the main chief just below, and I will go in this chapter by the same method for it is true that one finds more easily what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one on cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there are often evacuations of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake folly. For many kinds of people come for cures. If they come from those who aggravate their illness so that they die easily from the worsening of their disease, and from the greatness of their evil; and one should have fear of this.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give their opinion, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the disease is deceptive. It does not become that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but rather put greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open foolishly but wisely of what you are certain, and what you can have taken and lost; and use prediction and indication in the cures of your diseases where salvation may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and long memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord gives you good understanding and direction, and may you be willing to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here is the translation:
dou chief plein d’aigue	a full head of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	It is known that this illness often affects children at birth, and when the midwife holds the child's head too tightly; and sometimes it comes from a misplaced response that one does not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and nearly all those whom I have seen hastened to death; and therefore it seems to me that it is better to leave the treatment in the hands of some healers.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew so much each day that it could not be supported; and the moisture was so great that it became mortal, and this moisture is assembled beneath the bone under the siphac, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such that the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a large incision in the head; and let it be as long as we need, until the moisture runs; and see here the form of the spatula-like instrument:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make three incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the signs that you observe the swollen areas of each part, and the water flows out when you press with your hand inside, and it does not return: then it is necessary to make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture outside. Afterward, hold the incisions with drapauls and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then disengage, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head be comfortable, and give the patient dry food without much moisture until the limb is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you examine where the abscess opens, and assemble the water flow; for it never goes forward; never backward; never to the right; and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Here is the translation:
de reume	of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens that a disease called "catarre" occurs in the eyes or in the foot, and the disease is ancient, and the medical treatment does not profit at all, then the last resort cure is cautery with which one should cauterize the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, then, when you cauterize the veins, that the patient make his head back; after scrubbing the skin with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extracting the patient's neck to the entire .i. cloth; then look where the vein beats, and the eyes of one and the other are behind the ears, and are slightly reposed; then mark the eyes of the notch, then cauterize one and the other with a sharp pointed instrument of .ij. inches, so that the vein vein reaches just to the bone, and it should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, place the pointed instrument beneath the artery and cauterize below, cutting as if .ij. fingers are traversing.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, then the blood flows out continuously above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to feeling, then you must measure the quantity of the space of two fingers, then mark from the notch and make a cut just to the bone; and it is necessary to put blood flowing so it is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can suffer, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains on the bone point of the siphac, then cut that apostemes burst not in vain, then hold the wound and bind it, and the treatment of ointment until it is healthy.
de emigrainne	of hemorrhage
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old hemorrhage comes, and there is catarrh, due to the moisture of the eyes and the heat in the temples and old worn-out forehead and similar things, and it is treated by various methods of medical cures and all this does not profit him, if we cauterize the arteries of the temples and the burning heat, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs of their temples grow back, and attends to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is hardly restored except in some homes which are too cold; and if it is restored, then the patient removes his neck from certain cloths, then rubs the place with a rough cloth, and raises the place with warm water as much as the artery appears manifestly; then takes the spatula in the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then scrapes the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then raises it high as pincers, and separates well the tissues that are beneath each part; and if the artery is subtle, then turns to the point of the unguin, then covers according to the quantity of the .ij. heads. For if it is not covered, then does not know the without doubt all in all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draws out blood from the .vj. veins, just to .iij.; and if the artery is large, then it is necessary that you bind it in .ij. loops of a strong double thread of silk, which will not be visible before the closing of the wound, and will stop the flowing of blood; then covers the superfluity which is between the .ij. ligatures at that same hour, and then, if you see, then cauterize with a cutaneous cautery just to the bone as much as the heads are covered; and it is the mother work, if the patient has no fever and he is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid to finish the swellings: for this it is of great aid against the swellings.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the empty space with much cotton and places well-made tents; and when you remove them, then be cured by dry medicines that make the flesh grow, and by tents, until it is healthy; and if without cutting into the artery as you were opening, then hasten to cover with cautery, or fill the empty space with vitriol and hold with your hand so the blood is stanched; and if you do not have this present, then place on the empty space your finger until the blood is congealed, and raise the empty space of cold water until it stops, and be steady as it is necessary; and what is more mild and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cautery the vein with this trenchant .ij. parts, but the trenchant should be well spaced to wait longer for their healing.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, then they hold less of the blood.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And should have between the .ij. knives .i. a large space, and then when you have signed to incise the .ij. veins, and you place the burning iron on them until it reaches just to the bone, and covers the vein in .ij. veins; and should be separated between the .ij. parts because it is not surrounded by this cautery from all sides; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes fall from veins that are on the outer surface of the head due to fever, and it does not benefit at all from the medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient becoming inflamed, and feels as if walking in a fog; and since they are thin and moist so that the hairs of the papers are fallen, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, thus it needs a cure for this.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the old ones called it "confused cure", and it is that you make a row on the patient who has this disease the hairs that he has on his forehead, then make three equal incisions on the forehead according to its length; and let one of the incisions be as three digits deep into the forehead downwards to the nose, and the others three digits as three ribs above the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are as three ribs above the papers; and remove your hand from the continuation of the jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers at the joint.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and you will prepare a piece of sponge and much of fabric to suck out the blood, then apply the spatula bent at three parts from where it is in the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	Of the incision that is to be made at the temple up to the second incision; and scrape off all the skin that is between the two sutures to the entire surface that is on the bone, then make another part of the mean incision up to the other second, and then extract this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first suture the instrument called "scalpel", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and that's its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting edge towards the dry skin at the bone, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the mean suture. And cut all the vessels that come down from the head to the eyes as much as the incision continues up to what opens into the bone, and then make another part in the mean suture up to the other side; and then extract the blood equally, and press on the skin for the taken blood; then put in each suture a piece of old cotton, and put on soft cloths soaked in wine and oil and vinegar, and beware that abscesses do not come; and on the third day remove the dressing, and apply a great quantity of hot water, then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other cures as one cures wounds, until it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a person has a familiar catarrh, and you see the eyes are dim and small, and the vision is foggy, and the papers burn; and the hair falls out, and where the head aches in the front with a bitter pain, and the patient is exhausted; then know by these signs that those matters and that catharsis do not come from many veins, and the cure is more difficult than it is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is that you instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one equally large. And start from the incision on the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be just up to the bone; and hold your hand away from the edges of the temples that move to the grindstone; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then swab between the lips of the incision and put in a lot of cotton, and stretch tautly with linen thread; then lay on top a warm drapery soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to cause an abscess to form hot; when it is healed, you must rub the bone as long as the flesh begins to grow, then apply treatment of things that excite growth, which make the flesh grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take three parts of flour of wheat, and three parts of colocynth, and make a plaster; and apply it to these wounds to stimulate growth throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of these three things: either grains, or beast, or stone from the mine or similar thing like iron; or seeds, if they are yellowish, beans, peas; or flowing thing like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear stone or another kind of thing that does not adhere to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, if you distill a little violet oil or oil of sisament, then you will make extraction; and when you do this, and the nostrils are stopped up when you do this, and you put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and it is above the ear. Many times it comes out through this cure; and if it does not come out, then you will make extraction with subtle pincers, in which case this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that's good; if not, then you will make extraction with a subtle little double-edged hook; and if it does not come out through this, then make a cane of iron and put the head of the cane or opening of the ear strongly, and stop up what is around the cane with wax so that nothing can enter with the cane; then pull it out in the form, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, then take glue from what takes the ossicles, and put some instrument that is at a point to do this, and put a little cotton around; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever thing it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not know how to do all these things that we have said, hurry to open the ear thus that an abscess falls out with spasms; and the manner of the opening is that you first make the patient's head healthy, and extract blood according to its virtue, then place the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where it depends on fat or flesh; and let the incision be as wide as a moon, until you reach the stone, then scrape it out with your power, and suck hastily into your mouth; and continue treatment until they are healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer a spatula with a subtle touch according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and administer an incision of that grain. But do not do it when you think the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, so much that you have made many pieces; then extract with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Here is the translation:
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small-bodied, like a thorn and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large-bodied so that one can feel it, then one should assist in the extraction of pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and treat distillations, but the cure does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you examine the ear in sunlight: if no worms appear, take out the pincers subtly, and if they do not appear, take the candle of the form where it is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it is constricted below and wide above. And insert the most subtle instrument into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly all the way to the candle; do this as often as all the worms are seen. And if they do not come out, stop up with a cotton swab as I have said in the stone; and if they do not emerge as we have said, assist in distillations that the ancients have experienced in the removal of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this entire instrument, it is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is of silver or copper constricted below at a small opening, and above they are covered for distilling; and to press inside the distillation with an instrument of well-made copper, and if you see take the scraper and envelop it in cotton thread; then throw your oil or juice, and what you have of your medicines in the candle, and the candle is in the ear; then insert into the scraper all the cotton, and press your hand strongly so that the oil is distilled or extracted from the ear; and the patient feels it inside, and it is the distillations that are a little warmed by fire, as one distills in the ear; and take care not to make it too cold, for the medicine would not be good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have a small hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men through swelling of a wound, or when a piece of flesh grows inside the ear, and these swellings come sometimes from the front into the ear, if one cannot see them well; and sometimes it happens that the small hole is closed, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from the front, if one cannot see it well, is of great importance for the health in many dispositions, and in this case you must place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see apparent opilation, if the work has all this spatiumile of what is its form:
