ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize as it is said or according to the chapter on cautery, then heal with other treatments until they are healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot be opened, then cleanse the patient with a sharp and bitter cluster to remove what is in the foundation, so that it can open easily;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient takes a breath, and if the thread is pulled from the foundation, then it is an easy treatment;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them in your finger or with tongs, and grasp them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you apply the stitch according to this method: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is too large; and hold the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one to correct the excessive flow of blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a piece of cloth soaked in oil or rose water or cerote, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it be until it heals, and when they are healed, if they receive treatment of ointment and other treatments, until they are healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	you should search for the veins or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a searching of veins in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you make a point of a spatula or on an angle the scorching above, which does not let it get moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then the treatment as long as it is swollen as it happens;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot swell, then restart the rubbing more forcefully than before, as long as it hurts a lot and becomes scarred;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment as long as it is healthy.
dou fremit	for trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Here is the translation:
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the cold, and one feels it like a dead finger, and it comes into the whole body, and more in the hands than another part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread of an owl's feather, or a strong vulture's feather, and place that thread on the finger, so that the circles totally encircle the finger.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all around the thread so that you enclose the entire finger, and put it in the front, and stretch the finger out of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a ring of copper or iron in this form, and be subtle below and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, for you must hold to the finger, and press; And if you see, if you cauterize the frenum, as it is before or in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of theclyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make aclyster of silver or copper, or of tin alloy or maille; and never make these small and large instruments, according to those who are accustomed to them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that one uses in the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the small and large cluster is above wide, where the abdomen is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a separation or the abdomen is tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived from within; and it has a perforation on one side .ij., and on the other side .i.;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the abdomen be where one puts medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and let it be perceived entirely around small perforations,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and let there be between each perforation .i. a space of an inch, then put in these perforations .i. strong thread of twisted cord strongly knotted in .x. or around, and assemble the abdomen as if it were a sack;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is within, if he administers it with an instrument in front of a strong thread, then cauterize; and this is the form of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the cautery with oil or albumen of egg, or similar thing, then apply it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the minister holds it with his two hands together, so that it be fully visible, then extracts the cautery, and lifts the patient's legs to the partition.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to issue, let it flow as much as it can; and if he sleeps a night in total, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat him for a disease of bowel disorder, and the medicine hastens to exit, so recommend it as long as he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the morbid matters are at the bottom, or an abscess, so let the cluster be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the shape of the subtle cluster on which the skin should be held firm:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments with hands and medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing of stone, and cutting with a sword and a knife, or with a lance or a stick or a bramble, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or which are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if take care it's a matter of stone or similar things, and the skin is entirely broken and the wound is great.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you suspect a slight abscess: if it makes the headache worse from the cephalic membrane meanwhile it comes little blood from the wound, and the pain is on the contrary of the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and the patient is exhausted by an excess of wine and coarse meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to get better, let his meat be diminished, and do not drink wine, nor eat fatty flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, if abscesses or ulcers come, clean them with oil rose water softly, or in wine steeped.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no abscess or ulcer, put on the wound, so it is fresh in all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder, which I will tell a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has been moved, put on some ointments, so it may be healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a cut from a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by themselves, then assemble them by suturing, as I will tell about wounds of the belly, and the suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is discovered on the bone, and it breaks, and no longer holds except for a little, thus it cures; then heal the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat large pieces of meat, as if they are eating and roasting cooked food, like they are eating poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find rotten skin or putrid flesh, and it does not adhere to the bone, thus cut out all the rotten part, and throw it away, then heal it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has become infected in the wound or vein, without crust, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, thus cauterize the infection, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not benefit him, then he must be cauterized.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which soothes in such a way that the wound heals quickly.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; living chalk three parts, and powder subtly.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the poultice to the wound, and hold it firmly in place, so that it adheres well and joins with all its sap.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then leave it alone, and let it not become inflamed; for one does not stop the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes a poultice of hot chalk, when one does not have the incense nor the blood of dragon, but that the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has moved the wound, similarly in this case, then do not put this powder on it.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digested oils, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it has a good flow.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of other treatments until he is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then hold it steady with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the breaks of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between the two heads of the wound, but if the veins or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the veins, if there is no other remedy than to let them bleed, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the veins and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not to put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the veins is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be soothing, if you heat it in warm water, and mix it with rose oil, and cook it in warm water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other fingers of mine according to this manner, and wet bandages.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is swollen and full of pus, then pierce or cut below the swelling.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood comes out, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, for this is the practice.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is wounded, or the neck, and the conduits are guarded, because that's where the food goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the neck on the vein of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it firmly, and let it be for some days, then cure the wounds of the flesh thoroughly until it is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it out;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, if you pull them out quickly, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound purifies,
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be uncovered and aligned the joint;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then examine if the wound has become putrid, for the patient will soon languish: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not putrid, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put on the powder at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not penetrate deeply.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the body, and open the patient's eyes.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put on an attractive bandage, and bind it three times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, put much cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound three days, or two days, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there comes no spasm, nor evil trembling of heart in the translations of the vein;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good dispositions, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the wounds with tents and other treatments, until they are healthy.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and make an effort, especially if there is a fistula; if the treatment is as one must do.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or on the foot or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed on the bone, and has caught pieces, then clean the wound, and remove the false fibers if they are detached.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislocated, let the wound putrefy, then align the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and other wounds on other limbs are the judgments as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	because of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	From the great wound often bursts out a piece of intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, because of their internal insertion.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more painful, and often it is worse than the small wound that is the large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because when one puts back together the intestines in, one does not put them back together from hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestine swells so much that it feels cold, if they return to their place,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this it is necessary to treat the wounded place, because one must reset the intestine to its place like the others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in four manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common stitches have a place in the stitching of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitching of other wounds of the body and four other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and they are more prone to having a rupture of the belly, and I will describe one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine has fallen out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and a grievous thing is to put it back, this is by one of the three methods:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or by the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	for it is because the intestine is inflamed by the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is chilled, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soften a sponge or a cloth with water and apply it gently,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	where you cook in water simmering and steeping and infusion,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until the swelling goes down;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and sometimes this wine restrains, and it is murderous that one should not drink to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling subside, if you moisten the intestine with water or warm wine and bad humors are cooked,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for it is aligned, the entrance to a little of something;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound at the instrument of the thing which one takes hold of to stop the hemorrhages;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to deaden that which is cut,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we must not cut without great necessity for it;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments to make a division:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut deeply into the curve and do not digress, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it according to its natural form in its own place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	see if you can put it back, for that is worth a lot.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is located beneath the belly.
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and it is located beneath the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	Here is the translation:
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is on one of the parts.
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	if you make an incision in that case where the injured part should be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say for large wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use what you have prepared.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then you have between your hands, I minister pitifully who pulls all the treatment to his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it is the common manner of stitches,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	Then let the skin of the wound heal, I give you a space of an inch, and I fix a needle where it has a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and assemble the two heads of the siphac with the three threads in a bundle;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then he tightens with a double thread within the needle of the .ij. parts,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then assemble the .ij. heads of the wound together afterwards,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave .i. fingers' width of space, and he fixes another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then thread it like you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this according to what you have mastery of the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and be the moderate needles, between subtle and large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the subtle needles take hold of all the flesh, and those that are too large cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Because it is necessary for them to be moistened;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and soft skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not puncture and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then prick the heads of the needles, so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and you hold tight or wrap the heads of the needles so they can stay steady
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it takes only one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second cautery is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two heads of leather and the two heads of skin together on a needle or where it has a strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these heads all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then reset the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each vertebra, the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this vertebra belongs to the man,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I treated a wound that a man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which was caused by a blow from a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and it was a wound more than a palm large,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was a gut well inches two palms large,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and it was a wound within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I replaced the intestine then, so that it had been without food for twenty-four hours,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up to 15 days, and it healed, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had given up that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not heal from the ointment, for I stayed in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put cotton on the wound many times a day, and washed it with warm honey water until it was healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of cauterization:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and insert it into the defective part just up to the area within;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the right heart in the right way, if you have drawn out the blood or cauterized or wherever you inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make a piercing of another part of the defective area within;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this treatment is that you burn them thus as the pelleteer makes the pelz,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the syfac of one part, and take again from another, until the treatment is fully accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of treatment, which Galen says is proper,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	it is thus that some make, who naturally assemble the injured parts together,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the heads so that it faces another head, in such manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	fix a needle or head where the mirror-like surface, and make pierce that limb only slightly,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the heads thus face;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the part of the flesh just up to that spot within,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the head of the swollen vein;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make a piercing on one and the other side of the weak part just up to there within, in the other head of the swollen vein that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galen says this in his book, and no one testifies to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must cauterize the belly with .ij. needles, or it has thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push one needle from one side and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is the stitching more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus that the arsenic has not moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you put back in order the intestine, and sew up the cut; then apply the irritating powder, making a scar.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the arsenic has not moved, then apply no ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and they cut the vein, and sew up the skin, and the mirror;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound like the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, put them on, as soon as it begins to gather pus, a lot of cotton;
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and change it every day until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not have mastery of another medicine in many dispositions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you apply a light bandage in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it between the tendons, and beneath the bones;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or numbness in the belly, and it often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they treat with black wine clusters, and meanwhile the numbness reaches up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces inward, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the plaintiveness of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approaching of its natural disposition towards the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the serum flows from the wound, set it back as soon as possible, just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has turned towards black or green, then you must leave the black place, which removes blood that does not come from a vein.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then apply this to what is between the groin
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the joints in place during the procedure below the wound until it is far enough to alleviate the extraction when the nerves shout, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of a broken bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if one cannot restore it in some homes,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced by the point of a lance;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and thus obstructed the excretion and ventilation;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I examine a patient according to what I can see, and do not cease from subtly probing until he is healthy, and his eyes settle.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him settled, I doubted that the patient had a bad pain in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no point of pain, but remained in better disposition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	apply gentle heat to large wounds, then bring together the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the gentle heat has opened the mouth, then place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	if it draws back its mouth thus;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he covers the head, and it holds itself so that it cannot dislocate,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	Then set another fringe afterwards in that manner as before, so that the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head becomes stuck in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine thread that is very loose,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then bind it to the head of this subtle twisted linen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread on the needle, and sew the intestine, and reset it in its natural position;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of treatment of wounds is not better than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal tubes, if there is no ingenious remedy, better that subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when she is combed and made to bend.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the true nodulation of a hard and white abscess, where one does not feel pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is thus combed like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear and open wounds, and other times in dense ones;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes a little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healthy, and there is no flesh;
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	it is not except by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, through the small passage of blood or course;
ou por sa malice;	for his evil.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	for that which has hard flesh within, and on the lips, that does not let anything grow there.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there is too much swelling.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the flesh is porous, and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because for that reason the corruption is a kind of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where by its property in the region it slows down digestion, and delays health, and is harmful by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	or it is suitable that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by surgical operation of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	to the spleen, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to one of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is a fistula that does not obstruct just up to the place that I have said, and you are confident of the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you examine it carefully, if you take a straight rod of iron or wood, the fistula is straight, if it wants;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, it seeks a subtle probe of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the probes bend within towards the twistedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and you should make a fistula at the perforated hand and you cannot search very well by feeling.
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse through one of the perforations,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture flows from one perforation to another, and it purifies;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should examine carefully at your power, whether you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is separated in the font;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when you press with your hand, and the place where they feel it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, if the coping is according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the rotten flesh and corrupt humors that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is properly deep in the right place, it is necessary that you cut open deeply, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I often put warm compresses in medicinal treatment, and the stitches just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine corrodes the surplus which is accumulated at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then you put ointments on the wounds so they heal quickly;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it does not heal by this, then cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut around it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not grieve you in principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, then let it be so long that the decay is completely removed,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the things in the joints as much as it is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and render void what was before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not misled just as they found:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you discover and seek as long as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the limb;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot overcome it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if it has a small corrupt bone, and you can treat it with bandages,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the extraction is made with a suitable instrument for that,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if it has many bones, so extract them all, do not leave a single one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if you make the moisture contrary, there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you correct the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot dislodge them for an hour, then put on the wound a poultice which induces ripening,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the abscess is ripe among the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then if they have more lightly the bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a large bone, such as a leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you remove so much of the corrupted flesh that the blackness is entirely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corpse corrupt, it reaches just below the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if they want to sew and cover up to the corrupted area, and then heal as much as it is sewn;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you take an example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	It was a young man of around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the materials came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and did not have any cause of fever by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctor, in their foolishness, operated so much that the abscesses opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and corroded many materials, and became fistula, and there came many passages that all went bad and moist in the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a mirror mirrored cure within 10 years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they cured him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which corrodes through the openings to a great body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young boy became red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pierced a tent in one of these pores, and then searched for all the pores,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some veins came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut into one of the pores as much as I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came just to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	Here is the translation:
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and begin to restore the wound with medicines soothing by long tension, and cannot suppurate;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then began again, and discovered the bone as it was before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and the decay, and then stopped it, and thought to suppurate the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do so much that I scooped out a piece of the bone, and extracted it from all its marrow;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then the restoration of medicines; and he was quickly healed and relieved hastily.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it does not fail to restart the work because of the weakness of the patient, who cannot suffer.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often the evacuation of blood was successful, but he was entirely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and was born on the shoulder blade a hard callus, and was of good disposition and had no hindrance nor contradiction in everything, neither to the wing nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take the ligament, and stretch it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct him to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another bandage on the bigger one first, and bind it to the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stop the bleeding, if you extract the corrupt flesh from beneath,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the bone where you see swelling, so that the swelling does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a probe or a table beneath the bone to scrape out the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to cauterize as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and cauterize again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if it reveals the flesh entirely; then put the cauterizing iron underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then cauterize from one part to another the corruption, and be the healer who draws out the root of the corruption thus, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if there is corruption in the joint, then cut into the corrupted joint, and sew up the bone or whatever contains the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if there is corruption in the continuation of the joints, then there is no other anguish except to cut through;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if there is corruption in the prickling of the hand, or prickling of the foot, then it is very strong that thing,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however it is necessary that you inquire into that corruption, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and you must treat it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not work against you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the sockets to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the holes,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each similar appearance of work with its instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that you will show the instrument with which you will operate, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument with which you will operate, according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The heads perish either because of denseness or because of fever;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that corroding wound by the treatment of medicines, and it does not improve;
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you should cauterize that member up to the place where the corrosion comes from;
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by means of death, or through malice, which is a greater fault, of the defect of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are such that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards the blackness spreads, then it goes on to corrode the limbs one after another,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the entire body; if you hasten to copper,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is by the percussion of certain venomous beasts, like a sea scorpion and viper and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corrosion is at the head of the finger, thus the cupping, and do not give it too much space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, thus cupping at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, thus cupping at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it does not matter about the remedies that are applied, except for the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so we do it when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then it seizes after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, it seizes the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, then it seizes at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of coping with or supporting the limb is such that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch out one ministering to one of the ligaments below, and another ministering to the other ligament above,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you dissect the flesh that is between the two ligaments at a spacious interval, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cover or support, and place a layer of linen on each part, so that the supporting does not touch the healthy flesh,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another wound and abscess caused.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood flows out when you operate, immediately cauterize the wound hastily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you apply some retaining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then tie the limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I would counter that he had a wound on his foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a black spot which seemed to be burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first in his toe on the foot, so much that it consumed the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to amputate the foot, and was healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterward he returns to the corrosion or ulcers of the hand, and it comes to me
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on receptive things after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corroding;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he saw that I treated the hand, and I did not want, that I had hoped to counteract the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted also that if I cut off his hand, it would not die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was feeble; and he despairs all, and returns to his earth,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he stops using his hand, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not seen it happen except when one does another task, as one has need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never comes an abscess to the clear skin, and delays so long that it makes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they go and pierce, and in jumping the belly, and remaining with the vain views, just as one examines.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is above is as subtle as the delicate sheets of a drape.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not run just to the bone, nor just to the nerve, and such illness is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches almost to the bone in the forehead, then it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so that you should cut around the entire circumference, and similarly when it is subtle, just like a thin sheet.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not be afraid of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you find that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not on the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, if the treatment of the cyst thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look at the breasts are large, and the tumor which is in them is of foul odor,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then the medicated suppository of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take sage, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put skin in it, and boil it in a vessel over fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	as long as the medicine is red, and thickens also as much as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your necessity, and make it into water and into honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and cleanse the womb, and hold back the passages;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay there for two hours, then stir it in a sprinkling way;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the chest is exhausted, and the pus is evacuated.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time is it cleansed with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of wood from the vine, and throw water on top.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then cool it, and cleanse it, until you know that the chest is well purified.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, neither does Egyptian medicine help with ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if they treat him with a mixture of water and honey or he has a little bit of litharge broth;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	where you treat him with a mixture of honey and wine, which has the property of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the senses are well purified,

ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you cleanse with certain medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the breast is small, and the cane of the lancet cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if you enlarge it with a file a little, and put in a thin tent of Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or ointment of balsam, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut and let it heal so much that the lancet can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if they pierce where the swelling is above, whether it collects or settles below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the swelling is in depth, do not let it suppurate there;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut beneath the seat thus as you see,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it appears in such a manner that the swelling runs to the lowest place where it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the belly is perforated, if he does not let it swell up there
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the seat of the sinew below as you have seen,

pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then there is a gentle sewing under the other drapery according to the quantity of the hole,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the hole in the breast to align the suture, and do not remove the large drapery unless after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is above the pierced breast, often removes the swelling.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows that which runs from the swelling, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed of the patients who feel pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has extended in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps above the pierced breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	if you know that the senses are affected already, and approach the saints;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then dislocate it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open up the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if you change to another dressing, and renew the bandage.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the senses throw out undigested food after many days, know that the senses are not affected yet.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if you come subtle cors after long tension, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For the saints are approaching. For there are men who take long to heal their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the bowel is indigestible, it knows how to relieve itself after many days, it seems that the senses are not troubled;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the senses take long to clear, and are polluted, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	Here is the translation:
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a remedy made of ivory, and make it with rose oil, and the essence of old wine in equal proportion.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then boil it down and use it; and this same mixture makes cooked honey thickened,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when ivory remedies are not available,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then he applies a poultice, and spreads it over the breast, and sometimes he administers a long aristology.

si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if you treat a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that grows beneath the fingernail, near the joint of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	where they put their foot, or by chance not born with other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is weakened, and one does not take care of it, if an abscess comes to the foot;
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and throw so much that they run against the root of the nail, and by chance they run entirely;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come ulcers up to the bone, so that they bring putrid pain, and the skin is loose and wide, and the color is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat as we have said in the section, and the treatment does not profit at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluous tissue that remains around the finger,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are great aids if the bone is healthy, and the finger is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and he places his finger on the flesh, and begins to prick, and the blister.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	it is necessary that you put the straight edge beneath the finger that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the swelling above, and cut into the subtle and light flesh,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh of the medicine, burning and corrosive remedies to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of wounds until they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut around it, and remove the decayed part, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the decayed bone, cut around it in the same way as it was said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is injured, and bruised, and he feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the corner of the spatula-shaped instrument, cutting across above,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the incision does not reach just to the flesh which is beneath the corner, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain which comes from under the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two fingers that are born on the hands of certain men by chance are completely withered,
